  <script type="application/ld+json">
   {
					"@context": "http://schema.org",
					"@type":"Article",
					"url": "http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2014/11/12/video-of-dog-being-rescued_n_6144930.html",
            		"author": {
                "@type":"Person",
                "name":"Arin Greenwood"
				},
					"headline": "This Is The Moment That An Abandoned Pit Bull's Life Was Completely Changed",
					"articleBody": "It's just dumb luck that Lucy Rockdale happened to have her camera on at the moment she met Rio the dog and turned his life around so completely.

In late October, the grey pit bull was living alone by a river on the outskirts of Tracy, California. A Facebook user came across the painfully skinny pup, snapped a picture of him and posted it on the social network, tagging Rockdale in the post to alert her to the dog's plight. Rockdale, who's been involved with pit bull rescue for about five years and recently launched a local dog rescue group with her partner Ellen Barkley, was devastated at the thought of the dog out there on his own.

She drove out to where she thought the dog might be, using landmarks provided by some local fishermen, and she started to search. And search. And search.

First she checked under a bridge, then another one. Nothing. She then found some promising piles of excrement. But they, too, were a dead end.

&quot;Something told me to walk up the river along this dirt road and well, after walking maybe a quarter of a mile, I could see him sleeping in the dirt in the sun,&quot; Rockdale posted on Facebook, along with video footage of their ecstatic first moments together. &quot;His head popped up and like he had been waiting for me for his whole life, he came running to me....so excited to see a human.&quot;

(Story continues below.)
 (function(d, s, id) { var js, fjs = d.getElementsByTagName(s)[0]; if (d.getElementById(id)) return; js = d.createElement(s); js.id = id; js.src = &quot;//connect.facebook.net/en_US/all.js#xfbml=1&quot;; fjs.parentNode.insertBefore(js, fjs); }(document, 'script', 'facebook-jssdk'));
Post by My Buddy Dog Rescue.


Rockdale says that after she picked up the pup -- she calls him Rio, her &quot;river dog&quot; -- she &quot;threw him in my car, got in the driver seat and just broke down. I cried for him, I cried for the hundred others that are out there like him and I cried for dogs in general and how disposable they are to some people.&quot;

Rockdale and Rio take great selfies. Photo credit: Lucy Rockdale

Rockdale has saved about 40 dogs since her rescue group, My Buddy Dog Rescue, got started in September. Some of them have stories and medical problems that'll rip your heart out. 

There's a dog named Happy, for example, who was found tied to a cement pillar in downtown Stockton. Happy, it's thought, had been used as a breeding dog before she was abandoned. Her teeth were filed down, her stomach was bloated and her body was covered in bite marks. When she underwent emergency surgery after her rescue, the veterinarians found mummified puppies inside of her.

&quot;Happy is the worst I have seen. She really was dying slowly, and I can not imagine what hell she has been through,&quot; says Rockdale. &quot;She's a beautiful soul and deserves a wonderful home of her own.&quot;

Happy the dog with Lucy Rockdale. Photo credit: My Buddy Dog Rescue

Another recent rescue is Guardian. 

Rockdale got this dog after he was dropped at a local shelter. Guardian was in a wretched state, and the owners wanted him to be euthanized. He has also undergone emergency surgery, to fix his blocked intestines, and is now convalescing at Rockdale's home. It's just a matter of time until he's ready to be adopted out to the people who have already put in an application for him.

&quot;He is going to be fine,&quot; says Rockdale, who lives with her son and their two dogs, a roommate and his dog, as well as a rotating cast of foster animals.

 (function(d, s, id) { var js, fjs = d.getElementsByTagName(s)[0]; if (d.getElementById(id)) return; js = d.createElement(s); js.id = id; js.src = &quot;//connect.facebook.net/en_US/all.js#xfbml=1&quot;; fjs.parentNode.insertBefore(js, fjs); }(document, 'script', 'facebook-jssdk'));
Post by Lucy Rockdale.



Rio is something of a miracle. Despite the neglect he likely suffered in the past, he maintains a loving and trusting disposition. But even more amazingly, he didn't have any major medical problems at the time of his rescue. He needed to be neutered, but he was pretty healthy otherwise.

Rio has been staying at Rockdale's home for a few weeks now, too. He's learning the pleasures of trips to the dog park and naps in bed with his canine siblings. 

&quot;The best part about having him with me is just when I sit back and watch him be the dog he was meant to be,&quot; Rockdale says.

This arrangement was supposed to be temporary, but he's fitting in so well -- and no one else has asked to adopt him yet -- that it's looking more likely each day that the river dog is no longer adrift. Rio may have found himself safely, permanently anchored, at last.

&quot;There is a good chance I will keep him,&quot; says Rockdale. &quot;These dogs need us. We are their only hope to survive.&quot;

 Rio, left, with two canine members of Rockdale's household. Photo credit: Lucy Rockdale

UPDATE: After all he'd been through, Guardian didn't make it. Here is Rockdale's heartbreaking announcement:

Post by Lucy Rockdale.


Find out more about Happy, Rio and My Buddy Dog Rescue's other adoptable dogs on the group's Facebook page. You can also find information there about fostering and making donations. 

Get in touch at arin.greenwood@huffingtonpost.com if you have an animal story to share!

   <script>
    (function($){ // no Conflict
    $(function() { // dom ready
    var socialSubSearch = $('#social-subscribe-search'),
        search = socialSubSearch.find('.search'),
        newsletter = socialSubSearch.find('.newsletters'),
        rollout = socialSubSearch.find('[data-fx="hover"]'),
        liContent = socialSubSearch.find('.content'),
        searchInput = search.find('.input-term'),
        searchText = search.find('.text');
        var searchcheck="Huffington Post Search";
        var checkInputContent = function(evt){
        var inputVal = searchInput.val();
        if (inputVal != searchcheck &amp;&amp; inputVal != "") {
            search.addClass('searching');
        } else {
            search.removeClass('searching');
        }
    };
    
    newsletter.find('.content').hover(
      function(){
        var inputVal = searchInput.val();
        if (inputVal != searchcheck &amp;&amp; inputVal != "") {
          search.removeClass('searching');
          searchText.text(inputVal.slice(0, 3) + '...');
        }
      },
      function(){
        var inputVal = searchInput.val();
        if (inputVal != searchcheck &amp;&amp; inputVal != "") {
          search.addClass('searching');
          searchText.text('Huffpost Search');
        }
      }
    );
    
    search.mouseout(checkInputContent);
    searchInput.blur(checkInputContent);
    
    // rollover effects
    liContent
      .on('mouseenter', function() {
        var that = $(this),
            thatParent = that.parent('li'),
            inputField = that.find('input[type="text"]');
    
        if(thatParent.data('fx') === 'hover') {
          thatParent.addClass('hover');
          inputField.focus();
        }
      })
      .on('mouseleave', function() {
            var that = $(this),
                thatParent = that.parent('li'),
                inputField = that.find('input[type="text"]');
                
            thatParent.removeClass('hover');
            inputField.blur();
          }); 
        // end liContent
    });
})(jQuery);
   </script>

         Updated:
         <time datetime="2014-11-18T16:59:01-05:00">
          11/18/2014  4:59 pm EST
         </time>
        </span>
       </div>

        <!-- Print Icon for Canada and Quebect verticals in permalink page -->
        <a class="print_btn print_common" href="javascript:window.print()" title="Print">
         <img alt="Print" height="17" src="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/images/v/print_icon.png" width="20"/>

       </header>
       <!-- Article Text Body -->
       <div class="float_right padding_left_10">
       </div>
       <!-- Entry main text -->
       <div class="content" id="mainentrycontent">
        <div class="float_left">
         <!-- AD ads_sharebox_260x60 -->
         <div class="ad_share_box">
          <script type="text/javascript">
           if ( 'undefined' != typeof(HPAds.ad_sharebox_260x60_fix) ) {
              HPAds.ad_sharebox_260x60_fix();
            }
          </script>
         </div>
        </div>
        <!-- Entry Text -->
        <p>
         It's just dumb luck that Lucy Rockdale happened to have her camera on at the moment she met Rio the dog and turned his life around so completely.
        </p>
        <p>
         In late October, the grey pit bull was living alone by a river on the outskirts of Tracy, California. A Facebook user came across the painfully skinny pup, snapped a picture of him and posted it on the social network, tagging Rockdale in the post to alert her to the dog's plight. Rockdale, who's been involved with pit bull rescue for about five years and recently launched a local dog rescue group with her partner Ellen Barkley, was devastated at the thought of the dog out there on his own.
        </p>
        <p>
         She drove out to where she thought the dog might be, using landmarks provided by some local fishermen, and she started to search. And search. And search.
        </p>
        <p>
         First she checked under a bridge, then another one. Nothing. She then found some promising piles of excrement. But they, too, were a dead end.
        </p>
        <p>
         "Something told me to walk up the river along this dirt road and well, after walking maybe a quarter of a mile, I could see him sleeping in the dirt in the sun," Rockdale
         <a href="https://www.facebook.com/video.php?v=10204520139581373" target="_hplink">
          posted on Facebook
         </a>
         , along with video footage of their ecstatic first moments together. "His head popped up and like he had been waiting for me for his whole life, he came running to me....so excited to see a human."
        </p>
        <p>
         <em>
          (Story continues below.)
         </em>
        </p>
        <center>
         <div id="fb-root">
         </div>
         <script>
          (function(d, s, id) { var js, fjs = d.getElementsByTagName(s)[0]; if (d.getElementById(id)) return; js = d.createElement(s); js.id = id; js.src = "//connect.facebook.net/en_US/all.js#xfbml=1"; fjs.parentNode.insertBefore(js, fjs); }(document, 'script', 'facebook-jssdk'));
         </script>
         <div class="fb-post" data-href="https://www.facebook.com/video.php?v=822907947760056" data-width="570">
          <div class="fb-xfbml-parse-ignore">
           <a href="https://www.facebook.com/video.php?v=822907947760056">
            Post
           </a>
           by
           <a href="https://www.facebook.com/mybuddyrescue">
            My Buddy Dog Rescue
           </a>
           .
          </div>
         </div>
        </center>
        <p>
         <br/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Rockdale says that after she picked up the pup -- she calls him Rio, her "river dog" -- she "threw him in my car, got in the driver seat and just broke down. I cried for him, I cried for the hundred others that are out there like him and I cried for dogs in general and how disposable they are to some people."
        </p>
        <img alt="dog" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/2271274/thumbs/h-DOG-640x640.jpg"/>
        <center>
         <p>
          <em>
           <small>
            Rockdale and Rio take great selfies. Photo credit: Lucy Rockdale
           </small>
          </em>
         </p>
        </center>
        <p>
         Rockdale has saved about 40 dogs since her rescue group,
         <a href="https://www.facebook.com/mybuddyrescue" target="_hplink">
          My Buddy Dog Rescue
         </a>
         , got started in September. Some of them have stories and medical problems that'll rip your heart out.
        </p>
        <p>
         There's a dog named Happy, for example, who was found tied to a cement pillar in downtown Stockton. Happy, it's thought, had been used as a breeding dog before she was abandoned. Her teeth were filed down, her stomach was bloated and her body was covered in bite marks. When she underwent emergency surgery after her rescue, the veterinarians found mummified puppies inside of her.
        </p>
        <p>
         "Happy is the worst I have seen. She really was dying slowly, and I can not imagine what hell she has been through," says Rockdale. "She's a beautiful soul and deserves a wonderful home of her own."
        </p>
        <img alt="happy dog" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/2271658/thumbs/m-HAPPY-DOG-980x645.jpg"/>
        <center>
         <p>
          <em>
           <small>
            Happy the dog with Lucy Rockdale. Photo credit: My Buddy Dog Rescue
           </small>
          </em>
         </p>
        </center>
        <p>
         Another recent rescue is
         <a href="https://www.facebook.com/sastastic/posts/10204629539196295" target="_hplink">
          Guardian
         </a>
         .
        </p>
        <p>
         Rockdale got this dog after he was dropped at a local shelter. Guardian was in a wretched state, and the owners wanted him to be euthanized. He has also undergone emergency surgery, to fix his blocked intestines, and is now convalescing at Rockdale's home. It's just a matter of time until he's ready to be adopted out to the people who have already put in an application for him.
        </p>
        <p>
         "He is going to be fine," says Rockdale, who lives with her son and their two dogs, a roommate and his dog, as well as a rotating cast of foster animals.
        </p>
        <center>
         <div id="fb-root">
         </div>
         <script>
          (function(d, s, id) { var js, fjs = d.getElementsByTagName(s)[0]; if (d.getElementById(id)) return; js = d.createElement(s); js.id = id; js.src = "//connect.facebook.net/en_US/all.js#xfbml=1"; fjs.parentNode.insertBefore(js, fjs); }(document, 'script', 'facebook-jssdk'));
         </script>
         <div class="fb-post" data-href="https://www.facebook.com/photo.php?fbid=10204646480979829&amp;set=p.10204646480979829&amp;type=1" data-width="466">
          <div class="fb-xfbml-parse-ignore">
           <a href="https://www.facebook.com/photo.php?fbid=10204646480979829&amp;set=p.10204646480979829&amp;type=1">
            Post
           </a>
           by
           <a href="https://www.facebook.com/sastastic">
            Lucy Rockdale
           </a>
           .
          </div>
         </div>
        </center>
        <p>
         <br/>
        </p>
        <p>
         Rio is something of a miracle. Despite the neglect he likely suffered in the past, he maintains a loving and trusting disposition. But even more amazingly, he didn't have any major medical problems at the time of his rescue. He needed to be neutered, but he was pretty healthy otherwise.
        </p>
        <p>
         Rio has been staying at Rockdale's home for a few weeks now, too. He's learning the pleasures of trips to the dog park and naps in bed with his canine siblings.
        </p>
        <p>
         "The best part about having him with me is just when I sit back and watch him be the dog he was meant to be," Rockdale says.
        </p>
        <p>
         This arrangement was supposed to be temporary, but he's fitting in so well -- and no one else has asked to adopt him yet -- that it's looking more likely each day that the river dog is no longer adrift. Rio may have found himself safely, permanently anchored, at last.
        </p>
        <p>
         "There is a good chance I will keep him," says Rockdale. "These dogs need us. We are their only hope to survive."
        </p>
        <img alt="dogs" src="http://i.huffpost.com/gen/2272004/thumbs/m-DOGS-980x645.jpg"/>
        <center>
         <p>
          <em>
           <small>
            Rio, left, with two canine members of Rockdale's household. Photo credit: Lucy Rockdale
           </small>
          </em>
         </p>
        </center>
        <p>
         <strong>
          UPDATE
         </strong>
         : After all he'd been through, Guardian didn't make it. Here is Rockdale's heartbreaking announcement:
        </p>
        <center>
         <div id="fb-root">
         </div>
         <script>
          (function(d, s, id) { var js, fjs = d.getElementsByTagName(s)[0]; if (d.getElementById(id)) return; js = d.createElement(s); js.id = id; js.src = "//connect.facebook.net/en_US/all.js#xfbml=1"; fjs.parentNode.insertBefore(js, fjs); }(document, 'script', 'facebook-jssdk'));
         </script>
         <div class="fb-post" data-href="https://www.facebook.com/photo.php?fbid=10204668125400926&amp;set=a.1361709200660.2051917.1169472713&amp;type=1" data-width="466">
          <div class="fb-xfbml-parse-ignore">
           <a href="https://www.facebook.com/photo.php?fbid=10204668125400926&amp;set=a.1361709200660.2051917.1169472713&amp;type=1">
            Post
           </a>
           by
           <a href="https://www.facebook.com/sastastic">
            Lucy Rockdale
           </a>
           .
          </div>
         </div>
        </center>
        <p>
         <br/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <em>
          Find out more about Happy, Rio and My Buddy Dog Rescue's other adoptable dogs on
          <a href="https://www.facebook.com/mybuddyrescue" target="_hplink">
           the group's Facebook page
          </a>
          . You can also find information there about fostering and making donations.
         </em>
        </p>
        <p>
         Get in touch at arin.greenwood@huffingtonpost.com if you have an animal story to share!
        </p>

        </p>

                <p style="display: none;">
                 Justice is a 3-year-old boy who is super affectionate and loves playing fetch. 

Find out more about this goodhearted goofball on his adoption page.

               <li class="hp-carousel-item no-pin" data-beacon='{"p":{"event_action":"bottom_thumbnail_nav"}}' data-id="1" data-slide-id="4418796">
                <img alt="Aiden, Lilo's Promise Animal Rescue" class="lazy" data-src="http://i.huffpost.com/gadgets/slideshows/376294/slide_376294_4418796_sq50.jpg" height="52" width="52"/>
                <p style="display: none;">
                 Everyone just loves Aiden! This super cute boy with the adorable polka dots, goofy smile and pink nose will just steal your heart. 

Aiden is so much fun and will make you laugh all the time. He loves to play ball and dribble a soccer ball. He is all about the kisses and cuddling and is super snuggly. He loves to take walks and is great on leash. He is wonderful in the car, crate trained and housebroken. He also knows all of his obedience too! 

Aiden would make a wonderful companion for someone looking for an only pet not because he doesn't like dogs but because he lived with another dog that wasn't very nice to him. He is fine around other dogs and is very calm around them. No kitties; they are just too fun to chase! 

Please consider giving Aiden a chance, he is an amazing boy who would make a terrific best friend!  For more information, please contact Lilo's Promise Animal Rescue at lilospromise@live.com.
                </p>
               </li>
               <li class="hp-carousel-item no-pin" data-beacon='{"p":{"event_action":"bottom_thumbnail_nav"}}' data-id="2" data-slide-id="4413114">
                <img alt="Oscar de la Renta, Brooklyn Badass" class="lazy" data-src="http://i.huffpost.com/gadgets/slideshows/376294/slide_376294_4413114_sq50.jpg" height="52" width="52"/>
                <p style="display: none;">
                 Oscar de la Renta is a stylish Staffie mix who originally hails from North Carolina. He's approximately 3-4 years old and weighs around 70 pounds. 

Oscar's pretty mellow but would enjoy hiking, long walks or just relaxing by your side. He knows basic obedience commands, is crate trained, good on a leash and gets along well with people. He's quite affectionate and just likes to be near you.

Oscar has proven himself with all ages of humans and gets along with other large dogs. Oscar is neutered, up to date on vaccinations and microchipped. 

To foster or adopt, please visit the Brooklyn Badass website for an application.
                </p>
               </li>
               <li class="hp-carousel-item no-pin" data-beacon='{"p":{"event_action":"bottom_thumbnail_nav"}}' data-id="3" data-slide-id="4418962">
                <img alt="Tyrion, Hello Bully" class="lazy" data-src="http://i.huffpost.com/gadgets/slideshows/376294/slide_376294_4418962_sq50.jpg" height="52" width="52"/>
                <p style="display: none;">
                 Tyrion Pittister! He is a sweet, snuggly, goofy little boy who was rescued from a dog fighting case, and thanks to the Humane Society of the United States, he made his way to the rescue group Hello Bully.

Tyrion bears a lot of scars on his face from his past, but he is in no pain and totally ready to snuggle with a family. 

Tyrion is about 3-4 years old and still some some spunk so he gets all kinds of fun stuff to do! He loves to chew on nylabones, do enrichment activities, eat pupsicles and, most important, snuggle with all the volunteers. 

He is puppy-like when excited, and loves to run around in the play yard with tennis balls, and tends to snort extremely adorably. Tyrion's all time favorite thing to do is lounge on the couch or big fluffy dog beds with his humans. 

Tyrion is working on his polite ways with other canines and furry creatures, he seems to be extremely dog social. 

If interested please submit your application at www.hellobully.org/adopt or email ashley@hellobully.com for more information on Tyrion Pittister.
                </p>

                <p style="display: none;">
                 Pehu  is a 3-year-old cuddlebug who loves to snooze on your lap! He also loves to play, is a master of fetch the stuffed squeaky toy and has enough pep in his step to accompany you all your adventures. 

Penu enjoys the company of other dogs, playing and roughhousing with them until he's had enough and will come to you as his safe zone. He is food and toy motivated, and knows basic obedience commands.

               <li class="hp-carousel-item no-pin" data-beacon='{"p":{"event_action":"bottom_thumbnail_nav"}}' data-id="5" data-slide-id="4412226">

                <p style="display: none;">
                 At 10 years old, Princess the Shih Tzu needs a comfy place to settle down in. 

Princess still has plenty of spunk and enjoys dogs her size -- she has also lived with cats! She also loves meeting new people and kids, as long as they are gentle and not too rough with her. 

The Providence Animal Rescue League thinks this girl would be the perfect addition to a family looking for a constant companion. Please give her a chance today!

Find out more on Princess's adoption page.

               </li>
               <li class="hp-carousel-item no-pin" data-beacon='{"p":{"event_action":"bottom_thumbnail_nav"}}' data-id="6" data-slide-id="4418888">
                <img alt="Sophie, Lilo's Promise Animal Rescue" class="lazy" data-src="http://i.huffpost.com/gadgets/slideshows/376294/slide_376294_4418888_sq50.jpg" height="52" width="52"/>
                <p style="display: none;">
                 Sophie is a 2 or 3-year-old pit whose time was up at a local shelter.  

Sophie was thought to have been used as a breeder dog for profit, and was found in the attic of an abandoned home with her litter of puppies. 

Now that Sophie has learned that there is life outside being used and discarded, she has embraced happiness and fun!  

She is super athletic and has been spending time at an agility course where she has a chance to prove her innate intelligence.  

Sophie loves to be goofy and makes her foster family laugh every day. She is terrific with people and children of any age and other dogs that match her energy level. No kitties for Sophie, please!

For more information about sweet Sophie, please e-mail her foster mom at HSpeeks@msn.com.
                </p>
               </li>
               <li class="hp-carousel-item no-pin" data-beacon='{"p":{"event_action":"bottom_thumbnail_nav"}}' data-id="7" data-slide-id="4417870">
                <img alt="Rock, PAWS Chicago" class="lazy" data-src="http://i.huffpost.com/gadgets/slideshows/376294/slide_376294_4417870_sq50.jpg" height="52" width="52"/>
                <p style="display: none;">
                 Rock is a very happy-go-lucky 2-year-old Dachshund mix who loves to run and play. 

Despite his little size, Rock loves to sprint at lightning-fast speed and is sure to make you laugh at his goofy antics. 

Rock is extremely clever and even has a few tricks up his sleeve, like opening doors! He is very affectionate and loves to snuggle with his humans and follow them everywhere. 

Rock can sometimes be a little unsure around strangers and children, so he needs some time to warm up to his surroundings. He is looking for an experienced, adults-only home. He is also very cat-friendly, so he would do great in a home where he can have a feline friend to play with.

If you are interested in adopting, please call PAWS Chicago at 773-938-PAWS, visit www.pawschicago.org, or email adoptions@pawschicago.org.
                </p>

               <li class="hp-carousel-item no-pin" data-beacon='{"p":{"event_action":"bottom_thumbnail_nav"}}' data-id="8" data-slide-id="4413076">

                <p style="display: none;">
                 Jesse Pinkman's a loving and dashing pittie mix who's trying to put the past behind him. He's approximately 2 to 3 years old and a solid 60 pounds. 

Jesse loves to swim, cuddle, hike, play with sticks and do all of the usual dog things. He's also received top notch training and thrives with a strong and confident leader. 

Jesse's done great with his cat buddy, but we do think he'll do best in a home without other dogs or small children. He's a great, perfectly trained dog for the right pittie lover! Jesse is neutered, up to date on vaccinations and microchipped.

Find out more from Brooklyn Badass.

                <p style="display: none;">
                 Samson is a big bundle of love who adores cuddling. At just over a year old, he still has the sweetness and enthusiasm of a puppy. Samson is also a very active pup so he'd thrive in a family that can give him lots of structure and exercise. 

Samson is friendly with other dogs, and absolutely loves going on runs and frolicking in tall grass. He is house and crate trained and knows basic commands. He could go to a home with kitties with proper intro. 

Email his foster family at 518fosters@gmail.com to meet him.

(function() {
